‚óŹ Here's the shape of what I've planned ‚ÄĒ full detail is in the plan file:

  Your git question, answered: Tag the working SPI build as v0.1.0 now (your
  anchor). Then let risk, not size, route the work ‚ÄĒ the two Pi-side wins go
  straight to main in small commits (they can't break the proven path), and the
  transport rewrite lives on a feat/pio-parallel-link branch behind a
  --transport spi fallback until the panel proves it. Tag v0.2.0 as the reward
  when it works. The rule you keep tripping on: a branch is for changes you
  can't yet prove, not changes that are big.

  The overhaul, staged by risk (your choice):
  1. Vectorize pack() ‚ÄĒ replace the row-loop with a bitwise_or.at scatter;
  byte-identical (OR is commutative, shifts are disjoint), gated by verify.py. ‚Üí
  main
  2. Async PBO readback ‚ÄĒ 2-PBO ping-pong kills the glReadPixels stall;
  one-frame latency, primed in warmup, --no-pbo fallback. ‚Üí main
  3. 8-lane parallel PIO bus ‚ÄĒ phase6_parallel.rs (8-lane RX, reusing CS+READY
  framing ‚Üí byte-identical stream) + a C shim over libpio (ctypes can't call its
  static-inline API) + PioOut behind --transport pio. ‚Üí feature branch

  Two free catches along the way: the READY_PIN=12 log bug (real pin is GP26),
  and the C-shim requirement that changes the C-side effort for workstream 3.
  ‚éŅ ¬†User rejected Claude's plan:
     ‚ē≠‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ēģ
     ‚Ēā RayGLow: link overhaul + Pi-side render acceleration                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Context                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The Pi5‚ÜíRP2350 SPI link (24 MHz) is the proven throughput wall: ~46 FPS ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ceiling at                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 64 KB/frame, and FPS scales inversely with byte count (‚Čą55‚Üí30 as the    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wall grows) ‚ÄĒ the                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā signature of a transport bottleneck. The RP2350 PIO scan-out engine     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā could do ~1,000 FPS;                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā once the link is fixed, the next wall is Pi-side render overhead,       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā dominated not by the                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā fragment shader (16k pixels is trivial on the V3D GPU) but by the       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā blocking glReadPixels                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā readback and the scalar Python loop in pack().                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā This plan does three things, staged by risk:                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 1. Vectorize pack() ‚ÄĒ kill the per-row Python loop. Pi-side,            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā byte-identical, no HW.                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2. Async PBO readback ‚ÄĒ remove the GPU‚ÜíCPU stall. Pi-side, no HW, no    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wire change.                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3. Parallel PIO transport ‚ÄĒ replace 1-lane SPI with an 8-lane           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā source-synchronous bus                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (Pi5 RP1 PIO ‚Üí RP2350 PIO), killing the link bottleneck for good.       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Decisions: 8 data lanes (1 byte/clock ‚Üí byte-identical stream, zero     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reorder).                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Staged delivery ‚ÄĒ land #1 and #2 on main first; do #3 on a feature      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā branch with the                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā SPI path retained as a proven fallback.                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Version control approach (the git question)                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The right habit for a big architectural change is tag the known-good    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā state, then branch                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the risky work, and let risk ‚ÄĒ not size ‚ÄĒ decide what lands where:      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 1. Tag the current working SPI build first: git tag -a v0.1.0 -m        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā "proven SPI link".                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā This is the anchor you can always return to. (Commit the working tree   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā first.)                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2. Land the low-risk Pi-side wins on main (#1, #2). They're             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā verify.py-gated and/or                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā GIF-verifiable, ship over the existing link with no firmware reflash,   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā and are trivially                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā revertible. Separate commits: one for vectorized pack, one for PBO. No  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā branch needed ‚ÄĒ                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā they can't break the proven path (transport is untouched).              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3. Do the transport rewrite (#3) on a feature branch: git switch -c     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā feat/pio-parallel-link.                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā It touches firmware + new C shim + rewiring + lane-ordering bring-up ‚ÄĒ  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it needs the                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā panel to validate and must not destabilize main. Keep --transport spi   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā working the                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā whole time so the branch is always runnable.                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 4. When #3 is proven on the panel, merge to main and git tag -a v0.2.0. ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The general rule you keep tripping over: a branch isn't for "big"       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā changes, it's for                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā changes you can't yet prove. Reversible, independently-verifiable work  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā goes straight to                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā main in small commits; anything that needs hardware/integration to      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā trust lives on a                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā branch behind a fallback until it's proven. "v0.2.0" is the reward you  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tag when it works,                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā not the name you start under.                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ---                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Workstream 1 ‚ÄĒ Vectorize pack() (land on main first)                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā File: rayglow/render/hub75.py ‚ÄĒ pack() (~86-113) and pack_single()      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (~124-151).                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Replace the for y in range(WALL_H) scatter loop with a one-shot         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā vectorized scatter-OR:                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā g = lut[frame]                                   # (WALL_H, w, 3)       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uint16                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā r  = (g[...,0][:,None,:] >> _planes[None]) & 1   # (WALL_H, B, w)       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā gn = (g[...,1][:,None,:] >> _planes[None]) & 1                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā b  = (g[...,2][:,None,:] >> _planes[None]) & 1                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā packed = (((b<<2)|(gn<<1)|r).astype(np.uint16) <<                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā _shift[:,None,None])[:, :, ::-1]                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā fb3d = np.zeros((H//2, B, w), dtype=np.uint16)                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā np.bitwise_or.at(fb3d, _addr_row, packed)        # rows sharing         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā addr_row OR-combine                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā return fb3d.reshape(-1).astype("<u2").tobytes()                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Mirror for pack_single with _addr_s, _shift_s, _planes_s, uint8, H      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā rows.                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Byte-identity argument: same LUT/shift/plane math and same [::-1]       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reversal produce the                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā same packed[y]; the loop's |= and bitwise_or.at perform the same set of ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā OR ops into                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the same cells, and OR is commutative/associative so accumulation order ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is irrelevant. The                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (addr_row, shift) pairs are unique (documented invariant,               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hub75.py:28-29), so no bit ever                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā collides. Serialization is unchanged ‚Üí byte-identical. If bitwise_or.at ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is too slow,                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā fall back to a stable-sort + bitwise_or.reduce over the                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 4-contributors-per-addr_row groups                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (same result, faster) ‚ÄĒ but ship the obviously-correct .at version      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā first.                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Verify: uv run --with numpy tools/verify.py must stay GREEN (LUT +      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā two-chain + single).                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā During dev, keep a transient assert pack_new(f) == pack_old(f) over     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā random frames before                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā deleting the loop. Then python -m rayglow.render <shader> --dry-run 120 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā for a sanity GIF.                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ---                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Workstream 2 ‚ÄĒ Async PBO readback (land on main second)                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Files: rayglow/render/egl.py (add GL entry points) +                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā rayglow/render/output.py                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (Readback ping-pong) + a --no-pbo flag threaded through                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pipeline.py‚Üí__main__.py.                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā egl.py ‚ÄĒ add constants GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER=0x88EB,                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā GL_STREAM_READ=0x88E1,                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā GL_MAP_READ_BIT=0x0001, and bind (all core GLES3 in libGLESv2):         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā glGenBuffers,                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā glBindBuffer, glBufferData, glMapBufferRange (returns c_void_p),        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā glUnmapBuffer,                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā glDeleteBuffers. glReadPixels is already bound with a c_void_p tail arg ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ÄĒ when a PBO                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is bound, pass offset 0 instead of a client pointer (no binding         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā change).                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā output.py ‚ÄĒ Readback 2-PBO ping-pong: allocate two PBOs sized w*s*h*s*4 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā with                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā GL_STREAM_READ. In read(fbo): bind the current PBO and                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā glReadPixels(..., 0) (returns                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā immediately, async DMA into the PBO); then glMapBufferRange the         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā previous PBO, run the                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā existing box-sum‚ÜíLUT‚Üív-flip postprocess on the mapped view (the         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā LUT-index already                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā produces a fresh array, so the copy-out happens before glUnmapBuffer),  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā unmap, unbind, swap                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā cur/prev. Keep the synchronous path as the use_pbo=False branch         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (byte-for-byte today's                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā behavior).                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā One-frame latency: the PBO path returns frame N's pixels one read()     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā later. Acceptable                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā for an audio visualizer (~16 ms at 60 fps). Prime it: extend the        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā existing warmup                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā render (__main__.py ~163-167) to also do one read() so the steady-state ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā loop never                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ships a black frame. Expose --no-pbo (default PBO on) for fallback /    ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā timing accumulator                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā drops and FPS rises.                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ---                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Workstream 3 ‚ÄĒ Parallel PIO transport (feature branch, after 1+2        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā proven)                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 8 data lanes + 1 sideset clock; reuse the CS-framing + READY handshake  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā unchanged ‚Üí                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 1 byte/clock ‚Üí byte-identical 65536-byte stream (verify.py unaffected). ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Make it selectable                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā behind --transport {spi,pio} (default spi) so SPI stays the fallback.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3a. Firmware ‚ÄĒ new bin firmware/src/bin/phase6_parallel.rs              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Fork phase5_spi.rs; keep PIO0 engine (GP0-18), DMA ch4, framebuffer,    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā flip(), READY,                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā stall watchdog unchanged. Replace only the PIO1 RX program + input      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pins:                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā .wrap_target                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wait 1 gpio <CS>     ; idle                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wait 0 gpio <CS>     ; frame start (restart() zeroes shift counter)     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bitloop:                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wait 1 gpio <CLK>    ; data-clock rising = sample                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā in pins, 8           ; sample 8 lanes (IN base = lane0), MSB-lane first ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wait 0 gpio <CLK>                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā jmp bitloop                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā .wrap                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Keep ShiftDirection::Left, autopush, push_threshold(8) (now 1           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā byte/clock),                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Buffers::OnlyRx, clkdiv (1,0). in_pin_base = DATA0. RP2350b pin map     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (clear of                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā matrix GP0-18): data lanes GP27-34 (contiguous), CLK GP35, CS GP36,     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā READY                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā GP26 (unchanged). Pull-down the 8 lanes + CLK (E9 backstop), pull-up    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā CS. Keep a                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā const + assert! for each wait gpio literal as phase5 does. Fix the      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā misleading                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā READY_PIN = 12 const (real pin is GP26) while here.                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3b. Pi C shim ‚ÄĒ rayglow/render/piobridge/pio_shim.c ‚Üí libpioshim.so     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā piolib's API is static inline (function pointers in struct pio_chip) ‚Üí  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ctypes cannot                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā call it directly; a compiled shim linked against libpio is required.    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Flat ABI:                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pioshim* pioshim_open(const uint8_t *data_pins/*8*/, uint clk, uint cs, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uint frame_bytes, float clkdiv);                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā int      pioshim_send(pioshim*, const void *buf, uint nbytes); //       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā blocking DMA xfer                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā void     pioshim_set_cs(pioshim*, int level);                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā void     pioshim_close(pioshim*);                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Inside, mirror piotest.c: pio0 ‚Üí pio_claim_unused_sm ‚Üí                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pio_sm_config_xfer(PIO_DIR_TO_SM, frame_bytes, 2) ‚Üí build TX program ‚Üí  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pio_add_program                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Üí pio_gpio_init the 8 lanes + clk ‚Üí sm_config_set_out_pins(DATA0,8),    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā set_sideset_pins(CLK), set_sideset(1,false,false),                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā set_out_shift(false,true,8),                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā set_clkdiv ‚Üí pio_sm_init ‚Üí consecutive pindirs (out) ‚Üí enable. TX       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā program:                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā .side_set 1                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā .wrap_target                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā out pins, 8  side 0   ; present byte, clock low                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā nop          side 1   ; clock high ‚ÄĒ RX samples                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā .wrap                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pioshim_send = pio_sm_xfer_data(..., nbytes, buf) (blocking; one        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā per-frame burst, same                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā as writebytes2 today). Build: cc -shared -fPIC pio_shim.c -lpio -o      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā libpioshim.so                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (piolib built -DBUILD_SHARED_LIBS=1), documented like the               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā spidev/gpiozero note in                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā spi_out.py.                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3c. Pi rayglow/render/pio_out.py ‚ÄĒ PioOut (mirrors SpiOut)              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ctypes-load libpioshim.so (bind with explicit argtypes, egl.py:_bind    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā discipline).                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā __init__(clkdiv, ready_bcm=25, ...) opens the shim + a gpiozero READY   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā input on the same                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Pi GPIO25 (wired to RP2350b GP26). send(payload):                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ready.wait_for_active() ‚Üí                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pioshim_set_cs(0) ‚Üí pioshim_send(payload) ‚Üí pioshim_set_cs(1). CS via   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā gpiozero                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā DigitalOutputDevice (simplest), leaving piolib purely for the 8-lane    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clocked data.                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Pi GPIO map (BCM; clear of SPI0 8/10/11 and READY 25): data lanes       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā GPIO12-19                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (contiguous), CLK GPIO20, CS GPIO21, READY-in GPIO25.                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 3d. Transport factory ‚ÄĒ rayglow/render/__main__.py                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Add --transport {spi,pio} (default spi) + --pio-clkdiv. Replace the     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hardcoded                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā SpiOut(...) construction (~157, 169) with a factory selecting PioOut vs ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā SpiOut. The                                                             ‚Ēā

‚óŹ Memory saved. Now updating the index and implementing Workstream 1 (vectorized
  pack).

  A note on approach: rather than the plan's first-cut bitwise_or.at (which is
  often not actually faster ‚ÄĒ it's semi-scalar internally), I'm going straight
  to the genuinely fast form: each addr_row is hit by a fixed number of rows
  with disjoint shifts, so I group rows by addr_row once and collapse them with
  a single vectorized bitwise_or.reduce ‚ÄĒ no Python loop, provably
  byte-identical, and guarded by a module-load assertion on the grouping
  invariant.

  Wrote 1 memory (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Update(~/Projects/rayglow/rayglow/render/hub75.py)  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 11 lines
      82  _shift = (_chain * 6 + np.where(_half, 3, 0)).astype(np.uint16)
      83  _planes = np.arange(B, dtype=np.uint16)[:, None]
      84  
      85 +# Group wall rows by addr_row once. Each addr_row is fed by WAL
         +L_H/(H/2) rows whose                                           
      86 +# bit-shifts are disjoint (unique (addr_row, shift) pairs), so 
         +pack() can OR-combine                                          
      87 +# them with a single vectorized reduce instead of a per-row Pyt
         +hon loop. Stable sort                                          
      88 +# keeps the grouping order deterministic; the assert pins the u
         +niform-grouping invariant.                                     
      89 +_order = np.argsort(_addr_row, kind="stable")                  
      90 +_n_per = WALL_H // (H // 2)                                    
      91 +assert np.array_equal(                                         
      92 +    _addr_row[_order].reshape(H // 2, _n_per),                 
      93 +    np.broadcast_to(np.arange(H // 2)[:, None], (H // 2, _n_per
         +)),                                                            
      94 +), "pack(): addr_row grouping is not uniform"                  
      95

      11  class Readback:
     ...
       19      frame at scale 4.  Instead we integer-sum the s*s box (fit
           s uint16: 64
       20      samples * 255 max) on the *contiguous* RGBA buffer and app
           ly gamma via a
       21      precomputed LUT indexed by that sum ‚ÄĒ exact and ~10x faste
           r.
       22 +                                                              
       23 +    `use_pbo` (default on) double-buffers the readback through
          + two pixel-pack                                               
       24 +    buffer objects: glReadPixels into PBO[cur] returns immedia
          +tely (async GPU                                               
       25 +    DMA, no CPU stall), and we map PBO[other] holding *last* f
          +rame's pixels.                                                
       26 +    Costs one frame of latency (fine for a visualizer); the fi
          +rst call returns                                              
       27 +    a black frame to prime the pipeline. Set use_pbo=False for
          + the exact,                                                   
       28 +    zero-latency synchronous path (used by dry-run so the GIF 
          +stays frame-exact).                                           
       29      """
       30  
       23 -    def __init__(self, width, height, scale, gamma):          
       31 +    def __init__(self, width, height, scale, gamma, use_pbo=Tr
          +ue):                                                          
       32          if not 1 <= scale <= 16:
       33              raise ValueError("scale must be in 1..16")
       34          self.w, self.h, self.scale = width, height, scale
       35 +        self.use_pbo = use_pbo                                
       36          self._buf = np.empty((height * scale, width * scale, 4
           ), np.uint8)
       37 +        self._nbytes = self._buf.nbytes                       
       38          # LUT over all possible box sums: sum in [0, s*s*255].
       39          sums = np.arange(scale * scale * 255 + 1, dtype=np.flo
           at32)
       40          x = sums / (scale * scale * 255.0)
       41          self._lut = (x ** gamma * 255.0 + 0.5).astype(np.uint8
           )
       42 +        if use_pbo:                                           
       43 +            ids = (ctypes.c_uint * 2)()                       
       44 +            egl.glGenBuffers(2, ids)                          
       45 +            self._pbo = [ids[0], ids[1]]                      
       46 +            for b in self._pbo:                               
       47 +                egl.glBindBuffer(GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER, b)     
       48 +                egl.glBufferData(GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER, self._n
          +bytes, None,

          +lpha. Returns a

          +ed buffer)."""                                                
       59          s = self.scale
       35 -        egl.glBindFramebuffer(GL_FRAMEBUFFER, fbo)            
       36 -        egl.glReadPixels(0, 0, self.w * s, self.h * s,        
       37 -                         GL_RGBA, GL_UNSIGNED_BYTE,           
       38 -                         self._buf.ctypes.data_as(ctypes.c_voi
          -d_p))                                                         
       60          if s > 1:
       40 -            boxed = self._buf.reshape(self.h, s, self.w, s, 4)
          -.sum(                                                         
       61 +            boxed = rgba.reshape(self.h, s, self.w, s, 4).sum(
       62                  axis=(1, 3), dtype=np.uint16)
       63          else:
       43 -            boxed = self._buf                                 
       44 -        frame = self._lut[boxed[::-1, :, :3]]                 
       64 +            boxed = rgba                                      
       65 +        frame = self._lut[boxed[::-1, :, :3]]      # fancy-ind
          +ex -> fresh array                                             
       66          return np.ascontiguousarray(frame)
       67  
       68 +    def read(self, fbo):                                      
       69 +        s = self.scale                                        
       70 +        egl.glBindFramebuffer(GL_FRAMEBUFFER, fbo)            
       71 +        if not self.use_pbo:                                  
       72 +            egl.glReadPixels(0, 0, self.w * s, self.h * s,    
       73 +                             GL_RGBA, GL_UNSIGNED_BYTE,       
       74 +                             self._buf.ctypes.data_as(ctypes.c
          +_void_p))                                                     
       75 +            return self._postprocess(self._buf)               
       76  
       77 +        # Async path: kick this frame's readback into the curr
          +ent PBO (returns                                              
       78 +        # immediately ‚ÄĒ offset 0 because a PBO is bound), then
          + read the OTHER                                               
       79 +        # PBO, which has held last frame's pixels for a full f
          +rame (DMA done, so                                            
       80 +        # the map doesn't stall).                             
       81 +        egl.glBindBuffer(GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER, self._pbo[self.
          +_cur])                                                        
       82 +        egl.glReadPixels(0, 0, self.w * s, self.h * s,        
       83 +                         GL_RGBA, GL_UNSIGNED_BYTE, 0)        
       84 +        other = self._cur ^ 1                                 
       85 +        self._cur = other        # flip for next frame        
       86 +        if not self._primed:                                  
       87 +            self._primed = True                               
       88 +            egl.glBindBuffer(GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER, 0)         
       89 +            return self._blank                                
       90 +        egl.glBindBuffer(GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER, self._pbo[other
          +])                                                            
       91 +        ptr = egl.glMapBufferRange(GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER, 0, se
          +lf._nbytes,                                                   
       92 +                                   GL_MAP_READ_BIT)           
       93 +        if not ptr:                                           
       94 +            raise egl.GLError("glMapBufferRange returned NULL"
          +)                                                             
       95 +        mapped = np.frombuffer(                               
       96 +            (ctypes.c_ubyte * self._nbytes).from_address(ptr),
          + dtype=np.uint8                                               
       97 +        ).reshape(self.h * s, self.w * s, 4)                  
       98 +        frame = self._postprocess(mapped)          # copies be
          +fore unmap                                                    
       99 +        egl.glUnmapBuffer(GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER)               
      100 +        egl.glBindBuffer(GL_PIXEL_PACK_BUFFER, 0)             
      101 +        return frame                                          
      102 +                                                              
      103 +                                                              
      104  def save_gif(frames, path, fps, upscale=3):
      105      """Write dry-run frames as an animated GIF, nearest-upscal
           ed so a 256x32
      106      strip is actually eyeballable."""

‚óŹ Both Pi-side workstreams are done and validated on the desktop EGL. Here's
  where things stand.

  Done ‚ÄĒ Workstream 1: vectorized pack()

  - Replaced the per-row Python loop in both pack() and pack_single()
  (rayglow/render/hub75.py) with a grouped bitwise_or.reduce, guarded by a
  module-load assertion on the addr_row grouping invariant.
  - tools/verify.py ‚Üí ALL GREEN (byte-identical to the firmware golden, both
  two-chain and single-chain).
  - 2.1√ó faster on the desktop (1.23 ms ‚Üí 0.58 ms/frame); the absolute saving is
  larger on the Pi's slower CPU.

  Done ‚ÄĒ Workstream 2: async PBO readback

  - Added the PBO entry points to egl.py
  (glGenBuffers/BindBuffer/BufferData/MapBufferRange/UnmapBuffer/DeleteBuffers +
  constants).
  - Readback (output.py) now ping-pongs two pixel-pack buffers: glReadPixels
  returns immediately, and we map last frame's PBO (one-frame latency, primed
  with a blank first frame). Refactored the shared box-sum/LUT/flip into
  _postprocess.
  - Threaded use_pbo through ShaderToy; added --no-pbo; dry-run is forced to the
  sync path so GIFs stay frame-exact.
  - Validated byte-identical to the sync path, shifted exactly one frame (frames
  1-9 of the PBO run matched frames 0-8 of sync; frame 0 was the blank prime).

  Both changes are Pi-side only ‚ÄĒ no firmware, no wire-format change ‚ÄĒ so this
  is the "land on main" stage. The PBO win only shows on the Pi (the desktop is
  too fast to stall), so that's where to measure it.

  Your git question, concretely

  Anchor the proven build, then commit these two low-risk wins to main:
  git tag -a v0.1.0 -m "proven 24MHz SPI link"   # your always-safe return point
  # then, after you've tested on the Pi:
  git add rayglow/render/hub75.py rayglow/render/egl.py rayglow/render/output.py
  \
          rayglow/render/pipeline.py rayglow/render/__main__.py
  git commit -m "Vectorize bit-plane pack + async PBO readback"
  (I haven't run any git commands ‚ÄĒ that's yours to drive. Note there were
  pre-existing working-tree modifications from before this session; you'll want
  to review those separately so they don't get swept into this commit.)

  To test on the Pi: run your normal stream and watch the 5-second telemetry
  line ‚ÄĒ pack should drop, and render (which includes readback) should drop once
  the GPU stall is hidden. --no-pbo toggles the readback change for an A/B.

  Next: Workstream 3 (parallel PIO transport)

  This is the feature-branch stage, and per the plan it's gated behind "1+2
  proven on the panel" ‚ÄĒ because it needs hardware I can't reach from here: a C
  shim built against libpio on the Pi, new firmware flashed to the RP2350,
  rewiring, and a logic-analyzer bring-up to nail the lane‚ÜĒbit ordering.

  I can scaffold it now on a feat/pio-parallel-link branch ‚ÄĒ write
  phase6_parallel.rs (8-lane RX), the pio_shim.c + PioOut, and the --transport
  factory ‚ÄĒ so it's ready for you to build/flash/wire and bench. But it'll be
  unvalidated code until you're at the bench. Want me to start that scaffolding

‚óŹ That traceback looks scary but it's a one-line fix, and it's not a missing
  dependency ‚ÄĒ don't install pigpio/RPi.GPIO, they won't help (and RPi.GPIO
  doesn't even support the Pi 5's RP1 chip). The real culprit is exactly what
  you suspected: the mount. Let me explain the mechanism, because it's a good
  one to know.

  What's actually failing

  Look at the first error line, before all the fallback noise:

  xCreatePipe: Can't set permissions (436) for /home/will/rayglow/.lgd-nfy0, No
  such file or directory

  lgpio (the correct, Pi-5-native GPIO backend) uses a named pipe (FIFO) for its
  event-notification IPC. It creates that FIFO ‚ÄĒ .lgd-nfy* ‚ÄĒ in the current 
  working directory, then chmods it to 0664 (436 decimal = 0o664 ‚ÄĒ that's the
  "permissions (436)" in the message). You launched from ~/rayglow, so it tried
  to create the FIFO at /home/will/rayglow/.lgd-nfy0.

  But /home/will/rayglow is now your sshfs/NFS mount of the desktop folder.
  Network filesystems can't host FIFOs ‚ÄĒ mkfifo/mknod and the chmod semantics
  lgpio needs don't work over sshfs/NFS. So the FIFO creation fails ‚Üí lgpio init
  throws ‚Üí gpiozero falls through every other factory (rpigpio, pigpio, native
  ‚ÄĒ all expected to fail on a Pi 5) ‚Üí BadPinFactory.

  That's why it broke when you swapped the real directory for the mount, and 
  worked before. Nothing to do with your code or caching ‚ÄĒ lgpio just needs a
  local filesystem to drop its scratch FIFO, and your CWD stopped being one.
  Your ~/rayglow is the mount; /home/will itself is still local.

  The fix: launch from a local working directory

  python -m rayglow.render resolves through the editable install regardless of
  CWD, so just run it from anywhere local ‚ÄĒ /tmp is the conventional scratch
  home for exactly this kind of file:

  cd /tmp
  sudo ~/venv/bin/python -m rayglow.render
  ~/rayglow/rayglow/render/presets/will-helix.glsl --spi-hz 40000000

  The ~/rayglow/... shader path still points into the mount (root can read it ‚ÄĒ
  that's how the GLSL hot-reload already works), and lgpio now drops its
  .lgd-nfy* FIFO in /tmp (local ext4, FIFOs fine). sudo inherits your CWD, so
  the cd /tmp is what matters, not where the venv lives.

  If you want it permanent without thinking about it, a tiny fish function
  works:
  function rayglow --wraps 'rayglow render'
      cd /tmp; and sudo ~/venv/bin/python -m rayglow.render $argv
  end

  This will bite the Workstream 3 PioOut too ‚ÄĒ it uses the same gpiozero/lgpio
  factory for the READY line (and CS) ‚ÄĒ so the "launch from a local CWD" rule
  carries forward. Let me note it for next time.

  Wrote 1 memory (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Noted for future sessions. Give that cd /tmp launch a try ‚ÄĒ the renderer (with
  the new vectorized pack + PBO readback) should come up clean, and you'll see
  whether the two Pi-side wins move the pack/render numbers in the telemetry
  line. If lgpio still complains from /tmp, send me the new output and we'll dig
  further, but I'd be surprised ‚ÄĒ the FIFO-on-a-network-mount story fits every
  line of that traceback.

‚óŹ This is a genuinely valuable result ‚ÄĒ and it says the PBO optimization
  backfired on the real hardware. Look at the pattern: every shader is slower
  with PBO (the default) than with --no-pbo:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā    Shader    ‚Ēā PBO render ‚Ēā --no-pbo render ‚Ēā    őĒ     ‚Ēā

  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§

  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  PBO consistently adds 2.5‚Äď5 ms. Meanwhile vectorized pack is a clean win ‚ÄĒ
  pack is 0.6‚Äď0.8 ms, basically free now. So Workstream 1 stays; Workstream 2
  needs to be reverted to off. Let me do that and explain why it lost, because
  the why is the interesting part.

  Why PBO async readback is a desktop optimization that backfires on V3D

  The PBO trick rests on two assumptions, both false on the Pi:

  1. "glReadPixels is a hard stall over a slow bus." True on a discrete GPU: the
  framebuffer lives in VRAM across PCIe, and the sync readback blocks the CPU
  while DMA crawls over the bus ‚ÄĒ worth hiding. But the Pi's V3D is a tiled 
  renderer with unified memory ‚ÄĒ the framebuffer is already in the same physical
  RAM the CPU uses. There's no PCIe crossing to hide. glReadPixels here is
  comparatively cheap (a flush + a same-RAM copy into your cached numpy buffer).
  2. "You have other CPU work to overlap with the async DMA." The loop is serial
  ‚ÄĒ render ‚Üí readback ‚Üí pack ‚Üí send. The PBO defers the readback by a frame,
  but you immediately glMapBufferRange and process it, with nothing to overlap.
  Worse: the box-sum downsample now reads the mapped GPU buffer directly, and
  that memory is typically uncached / write-combined ‚ÄĒ streaming 512 KB of
  supersampled pixels through it per frame (scale 4 ‚Üí 1024√ó128√ó4) is far slower
  on the CPU than the sync path, which reads from an ordinary cached numpy array
  the driver filled efficiently. That uncached-read penalty is your +2.5‚Äď5 ms.

  So you traded a stall that barely exists for a slow-memory read that
  definitely does. This is exactly the kind of thing that only the hardware can
  tell you ‚ÄĒ good call running the A/B. Reverting the default now:

‚óŹ Let me smoke-test that the flag rename didn't break the CLI:

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Reverted and verified ‚ÄĒ sync readback is the default now, --pbo is opt-in
  (with the V3D finding documented in output.py so nobody re-attempts it
  blindly). The dry-run still renders clean and the flag is wired.

  Now let me read your numbers, because they tell you exactly where to push
  next:

  Two of your shaders are hitting the --fps 60 cap, not a bottleneck.
  will-circles and golfing-1 at --no-pbo sit at 59.8‚Äď60.0 fps: render 7 + pack
  0.8 + send 7.9 ‚Čą 15.5 ms, under the 16.7 ms budget. To see their true ceiling,
  run --fps 240.

  The heavy shaders are render+send bound, serially. golfing-6 = 16 + 0.8 + 7.9
  ‚Čą 25 ms ‚Üí 40 fps. will-blob ‚Čą 18.6 ms ‚Üí 53 fps. And send is 7.9 ms everywhere
  (6.6 ms SPI floor + ~1.3 ms READY/overhead) ‚ÄĒ that's your link, exactly the
  cost Workstream 3 erases.

  The correct version of what PBO was trying to do

  PBO tried to hide latency in the wrong place. The real latency to hide is that
  7.9 ms send is pure serial dead time ‚ÄĒ the CPU is just clocking bytes and
  waiting on READY while the GPU sits idle. Overlap it: render frame N while 
  send(N-1) runs on a background thread. The cadence goes from render + pack + 
  send to max(render+pack, send):

  - will-blob: 18.6 ms ‚Üí max(10.7, 7.9) = 10.7 ms ‚Čą 93 fps (from¬†53)
  - golfing-6: 24.7 ms ‚Üí max(16.8, 7.9) = 16.8 ms ‚Čą 60 fps (from¬†40)

  This works today, over the existing SPI link, no hardware. And it's genuinely
  effective in Python because the GIL is released during the spidev write, the
  READY wait, glReadPixels, and numpy ‚ÄĒ so the send thread really does run
  concurrently with the next render. It just needs double-buffering the payload
  so you don't overwrite bytes mid-transfer. This is the "right PBO": pipeline
  at the loop level, where there's actual overlappable work.

  A second, complementary render-side win: downsample on the GPU. Your render
  number includes reading back a 16√ó-oversized buffer (scale 4) and box-summing
  it on the CPU. A GPU downsample pass would shrink the readback 16√ó and delete
  the CPU box-sum ‚ÄĒ biggest help on the light shaders where readback, not
  shading, dominates render.

  Where to point next ‚ÄĒ your call

  - (A) Pipeline render ‚ą• send ‚ÄĒ software-only, works now, ~1.5‚Äď1.75√ó on the
  heavy shaders. The highest-leverage immediate win and the proper completion of
  the "Pi-side wins" stage. My recommendation.
  - (B) GPU-side downsample ‚ÄĒ cuts the readback/box-sum portion of render;
  medium effort (a resolve pass in the pipeline).
  - (C) Workstream 3 (parallel PIO) ‚ÄĒ eliminates the 7.9 ms send outright (‚Üí <1
  ms); needs the firmware branch + C shim + bench bring-up.

  (A) and (C) attack the same send cost ‚ÄĒ A hides it, C removes it ‚ÄĒ so A buys
  you most of C's benefit with zero hardware, which is why I'd do A next and
  keep C for when you're at the bench. Want me to implement the render‚ą•send
  pipeline?
‚úĽ Baked for 3m 22s

‚ĚĮ (A) first, the render / send pipeline. I will include a few more intensive    
  shaders next time to get a better range of samples as well.

‚óŹ Let me check threading import availability and what pin_to_core does (it
  matters ‚ÄĒ the send thread must not get pinned to the render core, or there's
  no real overlap):

  Searched for 1 pattern (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ pin_to_core pins only the calling thread (sched_setaffinity(0, ...)). So I'll
  create the send worker before pinning main ‚ÄĒ the worker inherits the full-core
  affinity and floats onto an idle core, while main stays pinned to the render
  core. That's what makes the overlap real instead of two threads fighting over
  core 0.

  Implementing now ‚ÄĒ first the import and the _SendPipe helper:

‚óŹ Update(~/Projects/rayglow/rayglow/render/__main__.py)

  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 59 lines
      146      sys.exit(0 if ok else 1)
      147  
      148  
      149 +class _SendPipe:                                              
      150 +    """Background SPI sender that overlaps frame N's transfer 
          +with frame N+1's                                              
      151 +    render. `out.send()` blocks for the SPI floor + READY wait
          + (~8 ms); running                                             
      152 +    it on a worker thread lets the main thread render+pack the
          + next frame                                                   
      153 +    meanwhile, so the loop cadence becomes max(render+pack, se
          +nd) instead of                                                
      154 +    their sum. Depth-1 (one frame in flight) keeps the added l
          +atency to a single                                            
      155 +    frame. Only the worker touches `out`, so the SPI/GPIO obje
          +cts stay                                                      
      156 +    single-threaded. The GIL is released during the spidev wri
          +te and READY wait,                                            
      157 +    so the overlap is real.                                   
      158 +    """                                                       
      159 +                                                              
      160 +    def __init__(self, out):                                  
      161 +        self._out = out                                       
      162 +        self._payload = None                                  
      163 +        self._work = threading.Event()    # main -> worker: a 
          +payload is ready                                              
      164 +        self._idle = threading.Event()    # worker -> main: pr
          +evious send done                                              
      165 +        self._idle.set()                  # start idle        
      166 +        self._stop = False                                    
      167 +        self._exc = None                                      
      168 +        self.acc_send = 0.0               # worker: cumulative
          + transfer seconds                                             
      169 +        self._thread = threading.Thread(target=self._run, daem
          +on=True)                                                      
      170 +        self._thread.start()                                  
      171 +                                                              
      172 +    def _run(self):                                           
      173 +        while True:                                           
      174 +            self._work.wait()                                 
      175 +            self._work.clear()                                
      176 +            if self._stop:                                    
      177 +                return                                        
      178 +            try:                                              
      179 +                t = time.perf_counter()                       
      180 +                self._out.send(self._payload)                 
      181 +                self.acc_send += time.perf_counter() - t      
      182 +            except BaseException as e:    # surface to main on
          + next submit()                                                
      183 +                self._exc = e                                 
      184 +            self._idle.set()                                  
      185 +                                                              
      186 +    def submit(self, payload):                                
      187 +        """Block until the previous send finishes (the residua
          +l send-bound                                                  
      188 +        stall), hand off `payload`, and return that wait time 
          +in seconds. The                                               
      189 +        worker transfers it while the caller renders the next 
          +frame."""                                                     
      190 +        t = time.perf_counter()                               
      191 +        self._idle.wait()                                     
      192 +        wait = time.perf_counter() - t                        
      193 +        if self._exc is not None:                             
      194 +            raise self._exc                                   
      195 +        self._idle.clear()                                    
      196 +        self._payload = payload                               
      197 +        self._work.set()                                      
      198 +        return wait                                           
      199 +                                                              
      200 +    def close(self):                                          
      201 +        self._idle.wait()                                     
      202 +        self._stop = True                                     
      203 +        self._work.set()                                      
      204 +        self._thread.join(timeout=2.0)                        
      205 +        self._out.close()                                     
      206 +                                                              
      207 +                                                              
      208  def run_spi(toy, watchers, feed, args):
      209      """Render + pack + ship frames to the rp2350b over SPI (th
           e only output).
      210

          -nder` dominates, the                                          
      279 -                # shader is. `pack` is usually negligible.    
      284 +                # send = the worker's actual transfer time (li
          +nk cost); wait =                                              
      285 +                # how much it leaked into the critical path. I
          +f wait hugs 0 the                                             
      286 +                # link is fully hidden and `render` is the cla
          +mp; if wait ~ send,

          +etical transfer min.                                          
      288                  spi_floor_ms = last_bytes * 8 / args.spi_hz * 
           1e3
      289 +                send_ms = pipe.acc_send / n * 1e3             
      290                  print(f"{n / (now - fps_t):6.1f} fps | "
      291                        f"render {acc_render / n * 1e3:5.1f}ms  
           "
      292                        f"pack {acc_pack / n * 1e3:4.1f}ms  "
      284 -                      f"send {acc_send / n * 1e3:5.1f}ms "    
      293 +                      f"send {send_ms:5.1f}ms  wait {acc_wait 
          +/ n * 1e3:5.1f}ms "                                           
      294                        f"(SPI floor {spi_floor_ms:4.1f}ms @ {ar
           gs.spi_hz/1e6:.0f}MHz, "
      295                        f"{last_bytes//1024}KB)")
      296                  fps_frames, fps_t = 0, now
      288 -                acc_render = acc_pack = acc_send = 0.0        
      289 -            # READY paces to the rp2350b's commit; also cap to
          - --fps so we don't                                            
      290 -            # render frames nobody asked for.                 
      297 +                acc_render = acc_pack = acc_wait = 0.0        
      298 +                pipe.acc_send = 0.0                           
      299 +            # Cap to --fps so we don't render frames nobody as
          +ked for (the worker                                           
      300 +            # + READY handshake otherwise self-pace to the rp2
          +350b).                                                        
      301              sleep = frame_interval - (time.perf_counter() - no
           w)
      302              if sleep > 0:
      303                  time.sleep(sleep)
      304      except KeyboardInterrupt:
      305          pass
      306      finally:
      297 -        out.close()                                           
      307 +        pipe.close()                                          
      308  
      309  
      310  def main():

‚óŹ Now let me test the pipeline logic with a simulated SPI sink (no hardware
  needed) ‚ÄĒ verify it actually overlaps, returns correct wait times, and shuts
  down cleanly:

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ The pipeline works exactly as designed (validated with a simulated sink, no
  hardware needed):

  - Send-bound case (render 5 ms, send 20 ms): 20.6 ms/frame ‚Čą the max, vs 25 ms
  serial ‚ÄĒ overlap saved 87 ms over 20 frames. wait = 14.4 ms (the residual ‚Čą
  send ‚ąí render).
  - Render-bound case (render 20 ms, send 5 ms): 20.5 ms/frame, wait = 0.0 ms ‚ÄĒ
  the link is fully hidden.
  - No deadlock, all frames sent, clean shutdown.

  What I built

  A _SendPipe worker thread (__main__.py) that owns the SPI send. Each
  iteration: main renders+packs frame N, hands the payload to the worker via
  submit(), and immediately goes on to render N+1 while the worker transfers N.
  Depth-1 (one frame in flight), so latency rises by exactly one frame. Key
  detail: the worker is created before pin_to_core, so it inherits full-core
  affinity and the scheduler floats it onto an idle core while main stays pinned
  to the render core ‚ÄĒ that's what makes the overlap physical rather than two
  threads fighting over one core. Only the worker touches out, so
  spidev/gpiozero stay single-threaded; the GIL releases during the SPI write
  and READY wait, so it genuinely runs concurrent with the next render.

  The telemetry line changed ‚ÄĒ how to read it

  57.0 fps | render 9.9ms  pack 0.7ms  send 7.9ms  wait 0.4ms (SPI floor 6.6ms @
  40MHz, 32KB)
  - send = the worker's actual transfer time (the link cost, as before ‚ÄĒ compare
  to SPI floor).
  - wait = NEW: how long the main thread stalled on the previous send. wait ‚Čą 0 
  means the link is fully hidden behind render (render-bound ‚ÄĒ the good case).
  wait ‚Čą send means the link still paces you (send-bound).
  - Effective frame time ‚Čą render + pack + wait.

  Predicted effect on your shaders (all render-bound, so wait‚Üí0)

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā  Shader   ‚Ēā Before ‚Ēā After (‚Čą render+pack) ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§

  ‚Ēā golfing-6 ‚Ēā 40 fps ‚Ēā ~60 fps               ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  The 7.9 ms send vanishes from the critical path. The light shaders
  (will-circles, golfing-1) were already at the 60 fps cap ‚ÄĒ to see the true
  ceiling now, run --fps 240. That'll also make your heavier-shader samples next
  time much more informative.

  This properly completes the Pi-side stage: vectorized pack (kept, ~free now) +
  render‚ą•send overlap (this). The PBO experiment is parked off-by-default with
  its findings documented. Files touched across the stage: hub75.py, egl.py,
  output.py, pipeline.py, __main__.py ‚ÄĒ these are the commits for main.

  that fast, even the heaviest shaders are purely render-bound. Give it a run on
  the Pi and send the new render/send/wait lines ‚ÄĒ especially curious what wait
  reads on the heavy shaders (should be near zero).

  on. Here's the picture.

  You're running single-chain, 4 panels ‚ÄĒ and the numbers prove it

  consistent. You're lighting a 256√ó32 wall (one serpentine row of 4 panels)

  ‚Ēā Your tuning ‚Ēā OE_GAIN 14, DIV (4,0)    ‚Ēā OE_GAIN 64, DIV (3,0) (your    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā                          ‚Ēā single-chain knobs)            ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  The crucial fact for Workstream 3: the entire SPI-RX path is byte-for-byte 
  identical between the two ‚ÄĒ same PIO1 program, same DMA ch4 byte-ingest, same
  READY handshake, same RX_STALL_US stall-watchdog + abort_rx_dma (that's the
  "resilience you cooked" ‚ÄĒ it rode out your mid-run reflash by dropping the
  corrupt frame and re-arming on the next CS edge), same flip(). So the
  parallel-bus RX widening (in pins, 1 ‚Üí in pins, 8) is the same delta whichever
  firmware it forks from; only the Display type / FRAME_BYTES / packer change.

  Two doc nits I'd fix while we're here

  - Stale frame-size comment: the A/B KNOB block says 8 = 512 wide, 128 KB; 4 = 
  256 wide, 64 KB. Those are the old u16 numbers ‚ÄĒ the actual u8 FRAME_BYTES is
  half (64 KB / 32 KB), as the very next comment block and your own 32KB
  telemetry confirm. The knob comment contradicts the code in the same file.
  - DATA_CLK_DIV MHz comments don't square with the (2,0)=37.5 MHz baseline
  stated elsewhere in the file ‚ÄĒ (3,0) should be ~25 MHz, not the "12.5 MHz" the
  comment claims. Worth a glance to confirm which is right (it's the internal
  pixel clock, harmless either way, just misleading).

  What this means for Workstream 3 ‚ÄĒ a real decision

  The PCB lands in ~5 days and flips you to the two-chain production wall
  (256√ó64, u16, 64 KB ‚ÄĒ where the link cost doubles to ~13 ms, making the
  parallel bus even more valuable). So WS3 ultimately serves two-chain, but you
  can't test two-chain until the PCB arrives. That's a fork:

  - Build WS3 on the current single-chain rig (my recommendation). You validate
  the whole parallel bus now on hardware you have ‚ÄĒ the C shim, the 8-lane
  wiring, the lane‚ÜĒbit ordering on the LA, PioOut ‚ÄĒ with one variable changing
  at a time. Then when the PCB lands, flipping to two-chain is a small
  parametric swap (Display1‚ÜíDisplay, u8‚Üíu16, pack_single‚Üípack), not a fresh
  bring-up. The transport is already trusted.
  - Build WS3 directly for two-chain (PCB-ready, but blind). Ready the day the
  PCB arrives ‚ÄĒ but then you'd be debugging the parallel bus and the new PCB and
  two-chain geometry simultaneously. Too many new variables at once; classic
  bring-up trap.

  I'd strongly do the former: prove the parallel link on the single-chain rig
  this week, fold in two-chain when the PCB shows up. The phase6_parallel fork
  would branch from phase_experimental (your live firmware), and I'd structure
  it so the chain selection stays a parametric knob so it isn't throwaway.

  Want me to (a) fix those two doc nits now, and/or (b) start the Workstream-3
  scaffolding on that single-chain-first basis? I have everything I need from
  the review either way.

‚úĽ Baked for 2m 24s

  ‚Ēā Build +    ‚Ēā piobridge/Makefile,                  ‚Ēā pin map + bring-up  ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā docs       ‚Ēā piobridge/README.md                  ‚Ēā order               ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Pi         ‚Ēā rayglow/render/pio_out.py (PioOut)   ‚Ēā compiles,           ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā transport  ‚Ēā                                      ‚Ēā SpiOut-compatible   ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Factory +  ‚Ēā rayglow/render/__main__.py           ‚Ēā wired; SPI default  ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā telemetry  ‚Ēā (--transport, --pio-clkdiv)          ‚Ēā unregressed         ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  It forks your live phase_experimental (single-chain u8), keeps the CS-framing
  + READY handshake + stall-watchdog identical, and only widens the ingest from
  in pins, 1 to in pins, 8. The byte stream is unchanged, so hub75.py/verify.py
  are untouched. The two-chain swap (for when the PCB lands) is marked at the
  three SINGLE-CHAIN lines in the firmware.

  What I could and couldn't verify from here

  - Verified on the desktop: firmware compiles; Python compiles;
  --transport/--pio-clkdiv parse; the SPI path still renders (dry-run). The shim
  is written against the exact piolib signatures I confirmed in the headers
  (encoders, sm_config_*, pio_sm_config_xfer/xfer_data, pio_select).
  - Can't verify here (no Pi): the shim compiles/links (needs libpio on the Pi),
  and the link runs end-to-end. That's bench work.

  Your bench bring-up (in piobridge/README.md, order matters)

  1. Build piolib as a lib: cd .reference/rpi5/utils/piolib && cmake 
  -DBUILD_SHARED_LIBS=1 . && make
  2. Build the shim: cd rayglow/render/piobridge && make
  3. Wire the 8 lanes + DCLK/CS/READY per the pin table (RP2350 GP20‚Äď27 data,
  GP28 clk, GP29 cs, GP19 ready ‚ÜĒ Pi GPIO12‚Äď19/20/21/25).
  4. Flash: cd firmware && cargo run --bin phase6-parallel
  5. Logic-analyzer first, slow clock (--pio-clkdiv 16): send a 0x00,0x01,‚Ä¶ ramp
  and confirm byte/lane order before any panel output. This is the one thing
  that can't be proven from the desk ‚ÄĒ the convention is byte bit i ‚Üí lane i (Pi
  out shift-right + RP2350 in pins,8 DATA0=bit0). If bytes land bit-reversed or
  lane-swapped, that's where it shows.
  6. Then on-panel vs SPI (must be pixel-identical), then lower --pio-clkdiv and
  watch rx fps/drops.

  --transport spi stays the proven fallback the whole time.

  Git grouping

  Two natural commits: the doc fixes (phase_experimental.rs), and the WS3 
  scaffolding (phase6_parallel.rs, Cargo.toml, piobridge/*, pio_out.py,
  main.py). The latter is the feature-branch work ‚ÄĒ feat/pio-parallel-link ‚ÄĒ
  kept behind the spi default so main stays runnable.

  When you're at the bench and hit something on the LA, send me the byte dump
  and I'll help reconcile the lane ordering ‚ÄĒ that's the one spot I'd expect a
  first-try surprise.

‚úĽ Crunched for 12m 7s

‚ÄĽ recap: Goal: speed up the rayglow LED-wall pipeline. We landed the Pi-side render wins and scaffolded the 8-lane parallel PIO link (firmware, shim, PioOut all compile). Next: on the Pi, build piolib and the shim, then logic-analyzer-validate lane order at a slow clock. (disable recaps in /config)

‚ĚĮ I've run into an issue while wiring: GP20 through GP27 are connected, there   
  is no exposed GP28 or GP29 pin on the rp2350b. GP27 is the highest GP number  
  pin.                                                                          

‚óŹ Ah ‚ÄĒ that's the constraint that matters. Your board only breaks out GP0‚ÄďGP27
  (28 pins), and the scan-out engine already occupies GP0‚Äď18 (12 RGB + 4 addr +
  clk/lat/oe). That leaves only GP19‚Äď27 (9 pins) for the link. Eight data lanes
  (GP20‚Äď27) would eat eight of those nine, leaving just GP19 for the three
  control signals (DCLK, CS, READY) ‚ÄĒ impossible. 8 lanes simply doesn't fit
  this board.

  The fix: drop to 4 lanes. That fits comfortably (4 data + 3 control = 7 of 9),
  divides cleanly into a byte (2 clocks/byte, no awkward bit-straddling that 6
  lanes would cause), and is still a big win ‚ÄĒ at clkdiv 2 that's 4 lanes √ó 50
  MHz = 200 Mbit/s ‚Üí a 32 KB frame in ~1.3 ms, far under your render time. The
  link still leaves the critical path entirely.

  New pin map, chosen to preserve most of your wiring ‚ÄĒ your GP20‚Äď23 data wires
  stay data; GP24‚Äď26 (which you'd already run as data) just get repurposed to
  control:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā signal  ‚Ēā RP2350b GP ‚Ēā  rpi5 BCM   ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā DATA0‚Äď3 ‚Ēā GP20‚Äď23    ‚Ēā GPIO12‚Äď15   ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā DCLK    ‚Ēā GP24       ‚Ēā GPIO20      ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā CS      ‚Ēā GP25       ‚Ēā GPIO21      ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā READY   ‚Ēā GP26 (out) ‚Ēā GPIO25 (in) ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā spare   ‚Ēā GP19, GP27 ‚Ēā ‚ÄĒ           ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  So on the RP2350 side you keep GP20‚Äď23 as data, and GP24/25/26 become
  DCLK/CS/READY. READY back on GP26 even matches the old SPI pin. Let me update
  the firmware, shim, and docs ‚ÄĒ and I caught a real bug while reworking the bit
  math (more below).

‚óŹ Write(src/bin/phase6_parallel.rs)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 61 lines, removed 71 lines
       1 -//! Phase 6 ‚ÄĒ Pi 5 ‚Üí RP2350 **8-lane parallel** link (Workstrea
         -m 3).                                                          
       1 +//! Phase 6 ‚ÄĒ Pi 5 ‚Üí RP2350 **4-lane parallel** link (Workstrea
         +m 3).                                                          
       2  //!
       3  //! A widened sibling of `phase_experimental`: identical single
          -chain scan-out
       4  //! engine, identical CS-framing + READY handshake, identical R
          X DMA + framebuffer
       5  //! drop ‚ÄĒ the ONLY change is the ingest data path. Phase 5 / e
          xperimental clock
       6 -//! one MOSI bit per SCLK edge (8 SCLK edges per byte); this cl
         -ocks **8 data lanes                                            
       7 -//! per clock edge = one whole byte per edge**, fed by the Pi 5
         -'s RP1 PIO block.                                              
       6 +//! one MOSI bit per SCLK edge (8 edges/byte); this clocks **4 
         +data lanes per edge                                            
       7 +//! = a nibble per edge, 2 edges/byte**, fed by the Pi 5's RP1 
         +PIO block.                                                     
       8  //!
       9 -//! ## Why                                                     
      10 -//! The 1-lane SPI link is the throughput wall: a 32 KB frame a
         -t 40 MHz is ~6.6 ms                                            
      11 -//! (~150 fps ceiling), and it only gets worse on the two-chain
         - wall (64 KB). With                                            
      12 -//! 8 lanes the same byte count clocks in 8√ó faster at the same
         - per-lane rate, so                                             
      13 -//! the link stops being the limit and the wall is purely rende
         -r-bound. The Pi                                                
      14 -//! side drives the bus with its own PIO (RP1, 200 MHz) + DMA ‚ÄĒ
         - see                                                           
      15 -//! `rayglow/render/pio_out.py` and the `pio_shim.c` it loads. 
         -CS framing + READY                                             
      16 -//! are unchanged, so the protocol is the same; only the width 
         -grew 1 ‚Üí 8.                                                    
       9 +//! ## Why 4 lanes (not 8)                                     
      10 +//! The board exposes GP0‚Äď27 only. The scan-out engine owns GP0
         +‚Äď18, leaving GP19‚Äď27                                           
      11 +//! (9 pins) for the link; 8 data lanes + DCLK + CS + READY = 1
         +1 won't fit. 4 lanes                                           
      12 +//! (4 data + 3 control = 7) fits with room, divides a byte cle
         +anly (2 nibbles), and                                          
      13 +//! still lifts the link off the critical path: at the Pi's clk
         +div 2 that's                                                   
      14 +//! 4√ó50 MHz = 200 Mbit/s ‚Üí a 32 KB frame in ~1.3 ms (vs ~6.6 m
         +s over 40 MHz SPI).                                            
      15  //!
      16  //! ## Byte order (why the stream stays byte-identical)
      19 -//! `in pins, 8` samples lanes DATA0..7 with DATA0 = bit 0; aut
         -opush at 8 bits = one                                          
      20 -//! byte per clock, byte-size DMA, in order. The Pi presents by
         -te bit i on lane i                                             
      21 -//! (`out pins, 8`, LSB-first), bytes in memory order ‚ÄĒ so the 
         -framebuffer ends up                                            
      22 -//! byte-for-byte equal to the same `hub75.py` packer stream th
         -e SPI path uses.                                               
      23 -//! **Nail this on a logic analyzer first** with a 0x00,0x01,0x
         -02‚Ä¶ ramp payload: if                                           
      24 -//! bytes arrive bit-reversed or lane-swapped, flip the shift d
         -irection or lane                                               
      25 -//! wiring. (This is the one thing that can't be proven from th
         -e desk.)                                                       
      17 +//! `in pins, 4` samples lanes DATA0..3 = one nibble; autopush 
         +at 8 = two samples                                             
      18 +//! per byte. Both ends shift **right**: the Pi (`out pins, 4`,
         + shift-right,                                                  
      19 +//! autopull 32) emits each byte LOW nibble first with lane i =
         + nibble bit i, bytes                                           
      20 +//! in memory order; this RX (in shift-right, autopush 8) reass
         +embles them to the                                             
      21 +//! exact `hub75.py::pack_single` stream. **Validate on a logic
         + analyzer first**                                              
      22 +//! with a 0x00,0x01,0x02‚Ä¶ ramp: if nibbles swap, flip ONE shif
         +t direction; if bits                                           
      23 +//! within a nibble mirror, reverse the lane wiring. (Can't be 
         +proven from the desk.)                                         
      24  //!
      25  //! ## Pin map  (RP2350b GP ‚ÜĒ rpi5 BCM ‚ÜĒ signal)
      28 -//!     DATA0..7  GP20..GP27   ‚Üź rpi5 GPIO12..GPIO19   (8 lanes
         -, IN base = GP20)                                              
      29 -//!     DCLK      GP28         ‚Üź rpi5 GPIO20           (Pi-driv
         -en data clock)                                                 
      30 -//!     CS        GP29         ‚Üź rpi5 GPIO21           (active-
         -low frame boundary)                                            
      31 -//!     READY     GP19         ‚Üí rpi5 GPIO25 (input)   (RP2350 
         -‚Üí Pi: armed)                                                   
      32 -//!     common GND (ideally a return beside each lane bundle ‚ÄĒ 
         -8 lanes at speed on                                            
      33 -//!     flying wire ring badly; keep them short and ground-refe
         -renced).                                                       
      34 -//! Scan-out engine pins are unchanged (GP0‚Äď18). DATA0..7 must 
         -stay CONTIGUOUS                                                
      35 -//! (the `in pins, 8` group); DCLK/CS are read by absolute `wai
         -t gpio` so they are                                            
      26 +//!     DATA0..3  GP20..GP23   ‚Üź rpi5 GPIO12..GPIO15   (4 lanes
         +, IN base = GP20)                                              
      27 +//!     DCLK      GP24         ‚Üź rpi5 GPIO20           (Pi-driv
         +en data clock)                                                 
      28 +//!     CS        GP25         ‚Üź rpi5 GPIO21           (active-
         +low frame boundary)                                            
      29 +//!     READY     GP26         ‚Üí rpi5 GPIO25 (input)   (RP2350 
         +‚Üí Pi: armed)                                                   
      30 +//!     common GND (a return beside the lane bundle; keep short
         + ‚ÄĒ lanes at speed on                                           
      31 +//!     flying wire ring badly). GP19 + GP27 are spare.        
      32 +//! Scan-out engine pins are unchanged (GP0‚Äď18). DATA0..3 must 
         +stay CONTIGUOUS                                                
      33 +//! (the `in pins, 4` group); DCLK/CS are read by absolute `wai
         +t gpio` so they are                                            
      34  //! hardcoded in the PIO program below ‚ÄĒ keep the consts in syn
          c with the literals.
      37 -//! Confirm GP20‚Äď29 carry no board-variant special function bef
         -ore soldering.

      36  //! ## Two-chain swap (when the custom HAT lands)
      37  //! This binary is single-chain (`hub75::single`, u8 cells) to 
          match the current
     ...

‚óŹ Now the shim ‚ÄĒ change to 4 lanes and fix the autopull threshold bug I caught
  while reworking the bit math: it must be 32 (one full DMA word = 8 nibbles),
  not 8. With threshold 8 the SM would refill the OSR after a single byte and
  discard the other 3 bytes of every 32-bit word ‚ÄĒ only ¬ľ of the frame would
  actually transmit. (That bug was latent in the 8-lane version too; good thing
  the rewire surfaced it.)

‚óŹ Hold on ‚ÄĒ while finishing the bit math I need to correct the RX shift
  direction I just set, and there's a subtlety worth getting right. The byte 
  must land in ISR[7:0] for the byte-size DMA to read it ‚ÄĒ that's exactly how
  the proven single-lane path works (ShiftLeft + threshold 8). ShiftRight would
  leave the assembled byte in the high bits and the byte-DMA would read zeros.
  So RX must stay ShiftLeft like the single-lane code; the nibble ordering is
  then the Pi's job. Let me revert that and handle the nibble order on the Pi
  side with a toggle (since the exact ordering is the one thing only the LA can
  confirm).

‚óŹ Update(src/bin/phase6_parallel.rs)

      16  //! ## Byte order (why the stream stays byte-identical)
      17  //! `in pins, 4` samples lanes DATA0..3 = one nibble; autopush

         - shift-right,                                                  
      19 -//! autopull 32) emits each byte LOW nibble first with lane i =
         - nibble bit i, bytes

         +te first: it does a                                            
      21 +//! cheap per-byte nibble-swap then `out pins, 4` shift-right (

         +to

‚óŹ Update(~/Projects/rayglow/rayglow/render/pio_out.py)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 8 lines, removed 1 line
      13  import ctypes
      14  import os
      15  
      16 +# Per-byte nibble swap (high<->low). The RX shifts left so the 
         +FIRST nibble it                                                
      17 +# samples becomes the byte's HIGH nibble; the Pi sends low-nibb
         +le-first under                                                 
      18 +# shift-right, so we pre-swap to make the framebuffer byte-iden
         +tical to the                                                   
      19 +# packer. bytes.translate applies this 256-entry LUT in C (negl
         +igible per frame,

‚óŹ Let me fix the memory note that still says "8-lane":
